< text>
The Staff have been very friendly and helpful. But the community is getting very dirty and ghetto, lots of trash everywhere, dumpsters overflowing, furniture laying around... Watch where you step, seems to be a lot of vomit in the parking lot... It's pet friendly but a lot of people not keeping their dogs on a leash and several vicious dogs as well. It's been several months after a wind storm and our roof got damaged, been reported several times and still not fixed, now there are squirles living in the attic. This place has fallen apart.</text>
<userid>104381811790220878952<//userid></record>
</dataset><record>
< Rating>
5<//Rating>
< gmapID>
0x80c3369ce0730ba3:0x99e73095a928547d< /gmapID>
<Pictures>None<//Pictures>< text>
My husband and I had been in search of an apartment for about a month and a half, we had inquired to several different apartments throughout the area, as well as other cities. We came across the Bel Air Apartment Homes, and we fell in love. We came across the community, on Apartments.com, and scheduled a tour, and I received a phone call from Alexis, just confirming our appointment and other details. We arrived to the office and we felt at home as soon as we stepped foot in the office. We took a self guided tour to the apartment we were interested and fell in love immediately. <Review>I lived at Woodsong Apartments for 1.5 years. While living there was acceptable, it was by no means worth the very pricey amount that they charged. The back pool was occasionally locked for no apparent reason, there were never TP in the pool bathrooms or seat covers and the womens restroom for the entire 1.5 years that I lived there was "under construction". Which really means it was locked and never going to be fixed. Try having two young daughters that need to use the restroom and are forced to use the mens with no TP or seat covers or soap in the bathroom. Great hygiene practices.

The windows in the apartments are old and are not double panned so insulation is always an issue. One of our windows did not even properly fit the window frame leaving a .5 inch gap. Our shelving in the pantry cupboards were warped and uneven, but I did not think much of it, canned goods are quite heavy so I understood that. Our carpet was not new but was recently "cleaned" which we all know means that the stains underlying the surface, stuck in the padding will arise to the top of the carpet again once walked on enough.

Upon move out, we had paid a $660 deposit and received $28 back! We left the apartment clean, paint was not required, and carpet in the living could afford to be cleaned again but that was it.

We were told that the entire apartment had to be cleaned for 5.5 hours at $25 an hour which totaled $120, the apartment was painted and so were the cabinets because the shelves in the kitchen were not protected which was $305 and the entire carpet had to be replaced due to "pet stains" which totaled $690. Funny because we had dogs but they never went in the two bedrooms nor did they have "accidents" in the living room. I was "prorated" small amounts of these bills due to the fact that the carpet was not brand new when I moved in and the paint had I lived there for 6 more months would have been fully covered. I find this to be amazing because I have never lived in an apartment where I had to pay for paint and cleaning, that is called normal wear and tear and part of the business. Carpet cleaning yes, replacement no.

You don't even want to know about the outside water, trash and sewer company they use. Which forces you to get paper statements, pay an extra 5$ a month for that paper statement and upon move out they tack on a statement closing charge of $7. Please tell me how for my tiny apartment I pay more in water and trash a month than my parents do for a 1200 square foot home on an 8000 square foot lot with beautiful grass??? We pay on average between $55-$60 a month! Um Hello!! Water and trash is an every other month bill and is not that much money!!!!! Oh but according to the apartments we don't pay for water for the grass out in the grounds for the apartments. But how come the gardeners can put their trash in the trash can that I pay for? How come when a resident moves out you don't have a special large pick up for that dumb person that left all of their stuff, but instead the facilities maintenance crew puts all of that junk in the trash that I pay for? Hmmm. Something tells me that this LLC is running a business with protocols that simply don't add up.

If you ask me, this place is a scam when it comes to your deposit and they fully take advantage of their residents. I will be happy to post our stream of email communication once I have resolved my case with the Fusion LLC corporate office.< /Review>< pictures>

First of all, thank you for the reasonable prices. When I saw the prices I didn't expect to get this kind of taste. But it was ridiculously tasty. <Rating>5</Rating><Review>As the child of a Salvadorian mother, I grew up with Salvadorian food and it's something I've grown accustomed to. That said, I'm always apprehensive about pupusas when eating out. My mom's pupusas will always be the best to me, but the pupusas here are well done.

I especially enjoy that they offer casamiento, which was delicious. The chorizo offered here was new to me, but was also very good, served on a sizzling skillet. The horchata was good and the authentic Central American stuff, which can be hard to find. It was definitely much sweeter than what I'm used to, so that is something to keep in mind.<//Review><Pics>None< /Pics><response>None< /response>< gmap_id>
